## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear oscillators. Common models include linear damping, nonlinear restoring forces (e.g., Duffing), self-excited damping (van der Pol/Rayleigh), and periodic/parametric forcing via explicit t-dependence.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear mass-spring-damper (state-space): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (small oscillations with linear restoring force and viscous damping; signs absorbed into c0,c1)
- Conservative oscillator from potential: dv_dt = -dU_dx(x) where dU_dx(x) ≈ c0 * x (energy-conserving case; no explicit v,t dependence)
- Cubic (Duffing) restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with linear damping)
- Quintic stiffening: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order restoring nonlinearity near large amplitudes)
- Pendulum-like restoring: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (angular oscillator with sinusoidal restoring torque plus damping)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) drag: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (fluid-like drag where dissipation grows with speed)
- Nonlinear stiffness-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v + c2 * x (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle via negative damping at small |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v + c2 * x (self-excitation with velocity-dependent damping)
- Externally forced oscillator (harmonic forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic drive)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear resonance, bistability)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; Mathieu-type behavior)
- Non-smooth/impact-like restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * Abs(x) * x (piecewise-stiffening restoring force via |x|x)
- Rational softening/hardening restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x / (c2 + x**2) + c3 * v (bounded effective stiffness at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative vs dissipative identification: absence of v terms suggests (approximately) energy-conserving dynamics; presence of terms proportional to v, v|v|, or x^2 v indicates damping/dissipation mechanisms.
- Odd symmetry of restoring force: for many centered oscillators, dv_dt as a function of x is predominantly odd (x, x^3, sin(c*x), |x|x), reflecting symmetric potentials about x=0.
- Hardening/softening stiffness: positive vs negative cubic-in-x contributions (x**3) shift the oscillation frequency with amplitude and can create multi-stability under forcing.
- Self-excited limit cycles: factors like (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing a stable oscillation amplitude.
- External periodic forcing: additive cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms generate driven resonance; response may include frequency locking and harmonics.
- Parametric resonance signature: time-varying stiffness multiplying x, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, is characteristic of Mathieu/parametric excitation behavior.
- Nonlinear drag scaling: v*Abs(v) (quadratic drag) suggests high-Reynolds-number-like dissipation, whereas linear v suggests viscous/low-speed dissipation.
- Amplitude-dependent dissipation: x**2*v or higher-order couplings imply damping increases with displacement amplitude (material or geometric nonlinear losses).

GT: -alpha*v**c0 - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x - omega0**c4*x*exp(-Abs(x))

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v*(1 - x²) - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

Expanding: `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v + 0.725306*v*x² - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³` (coefficient ≈ -0.0892)
2. `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.7253)
3. `v*x²` (coefficient ≈ 0.7253)
4. `x` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)
5. `x*exp(-|x|)` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)

The key challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)`. This function cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, `x*|x|`, `log`, `Max`, or other non-exponential basis functions. Let me check which candidates contain `x*exp(...)` terms.

**Key observation:** `x*exp(-|x|)` is the critical term. Let me identify candidates that could potentially represent it:

- Candidates with `x*exp(c*|x|)`: **33, 45, 47, 48** (these have `x*exp(c*Abs(x))`)
- All other candidates use polynomial/`|x|`/`Max`/`log` basis functions which cannot exactly match `x*exp(-|x|)`.

Let me analyze the promising candidates:

**Candidate 33:** `c0 + c1*v³ + c2*v + c3*v*x² + c4*x*|x| + c5*x⁵ + c6*x*exp(c7*|x|)`
- Set c7 = -1: gives `x*exp(-|x|)`. Has v³, v, v*x², x*exp(-|x|). But needs an `x` term and has `x*|x|` and `x⁵` instead. Missing standalone `x` term (c0 is a constant, not x). Cannot produce the `x` term. **NO MATCH.**

Wait - actually c4*x*|x| when x>0 gives c4*x², when x<0 gives -c4*x². This is not the same as `x`. So candidate 33 is missing the `x` term entirely.

**Candidate 45:** `c0*v³ + c1*v + c2*v*x² + c3*x*|x| + c4*x⁵ + c5*x*exp(c6*|x|) + x`
- Has: v³, v, v*x², x*|x|, x⁵, x*exp(c6*|x|), x (fixed coefficient 1)
- Set c6=-1. The `x` term has fixed coefficient 1, but GT needs ≈-1.4474. We can't adjust it. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 47:** `c0*x + c1*v³ + c2*v + c3*v*x² + c4*x*|x| + c5*x⁵ + c6*x*exp(c7*|x|) + c8*x + c9`
- Has: (c0+c8)*x, v³, v, v*x², x*|x|, x⁵, x*exp(c7*|x|), constant c9
- Set c7=-1, c9=0, c4=0, c5=0. Then: (c0+c8)*x + c1*v³ + c2*v + c3*v*x² + c6*x*exp(-|x|)
